<header class="hero">
  <div class="hero-inner">
    <div class="hero-tag">Interactive Health Data Brief</div>
    <h1>The Geography of Obesity:<br>How Food Insecurity and Rurality Shape <em>America's Health</em></h1>
    <p class="subtitle">Across 2,638 U.S. counties, a troubling pattern emerges: where you live may determine how healthy you can be. This analysis explores the compound disadvantages facing rural communities with high food insecurity.</p>
    <div class="rq">
      <div class="rq-label">Research Question</div>
      <p>Do rural counties with high food insecurity face compounded obesity challenges, and how do food insecurity and rural geography jointly influence county-level obesity rates?</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</header>

<section id="intro">
  <div class="container narrow">
    <div class="section-label">Introduction</div>
    <h2>A Tale of Two Americas</h2>
    <p class="lead">In Humphreys County, Mississippi&mdash;a place where every single resident lives in a rural area and nearly one in five are food insecure&mdash;the adult obesity rate stands at 52.4%, the highest in the nation. Meanwhile, in urban Marin County, California, just 19.2% of adults are obese. This 33-percentage-point chasm between two American counties is not a matter of personal choice alone; it is a story written in geography, infrastructure, and access.</p>
    <p>Obesity affects over 40% of American adults and costs the U.S. healthcare system an estimated $173 billion annually. While individual behavior plays a role, a growing body of research points to structural and environmental factors&mdash;particularly food insecurity and geographic isolation&mdash;as powerful drivers of health disparities. This data brief examines 2,638 U.S. counties to investigate how rurality and food insecurity combine to shape obesity outcomes.</p>
    <div class="stats-row">
      <div class="stat-card"><div class="num">37.7%</div><div class="label">Average county-level<br>obesity rate</div></div>
      <div class="stat-card"><div class="num">2,638</div><div class="label">Counties analyzed<br>across the U.S.</div></div>
      <div class="stat-card"><div class="num">61.0%</div><div class="label">Rural counties above<br>national obesity avg</div></div>
      <div class="stat-card"><div class="num">r = 0.43</div><div class="label">Correlation: food<br>insecurity &amp; obesity</div></div>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>

<section class="alt">
  <div class="container narrow">
    <div class="section-label">Data &amp; Methods</div>
    <h2>How We Analyzed the Data</h2>
    <p>This analysis merges two publicly available datasets at the county level using FIPS codes as a common identifier. The <strong>2024 County Health Rankings</strong> dataset, compiled by the University of Wisconsin Population Health Institute in collaboration with the Robert Wood Johnson Foundation, provides over 60 health, demographic, and socioeconomic indicators for nearly every U.S. county&mdash;including food insecurity and rural population percentages. The <strong>CDC PLACES 2025</strong> dataset supplies county-level obesity prevalence estimates derived from the Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System (BRFSS). Three key variables guide this analysis: (1) adult obesity prevalence (crude percentage), (2) the percentage of food-insecure residents, and (3) the percentage of the county population living in rural areas. Together, these variables allow us to explore whether geographic isolation and food insecurity produce compounding health disadvantages.</p>
  </div>
</section>

<section id="viz1">
  <div class="container">
    <div class="section-label">Interactive Visualization 1</div>
    <h2>Mapping the Three-Way Relationship</h2>
    <p>The scatter plot below shows each county as a point, with rurality on the x-axis and obesity on the y-axis. The color of each dot represents the level of food insecurity&mdash;darker reds signal higher food insecurity. Use the filters to explore patterns by state or region.</p>
    <div class="viz-card">
      <h3>County-Level Obesity vs. Rurality</h3>
      <p class="viz-desc">Each dot is one county. Color intensity shows food insecurity (%). Hover for details.</p>
      <div class="viz-controls">
        <div><label for="region-filter">Region: </label><select id="region-filter"><option value="All">All Regions</option><option value="South">South</option><option value="Midwest">Midwest</option><option value="Northeast">Northeast</option><option value="West">West</option></select></div>
        <div><label for="state-filter">State: </label><select id="state-filter"><option value="All">All States</option></select></div>
        <div><label for="fi-filter">Food Insecurity: </label><select id="fi-filter"><option value="All">All Levels</option><option value="low">Low (&lt;8%)</option><option value="med">Medium (8-15%)</option><option value="high">High (&gt;15%)</option></select></div>
      </div>
      <div id="scatter-plot" style="width:100%;height:500px;"></div>
    </div>
    <div class="finding"><div class="finding-icon">1</div><div><p><strong>Rurality and obesity are positively correlated (r&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.30).</strong> Counties in the most rural quintile (100% rural population) average an obesity rate of 38.2%, compared with 35.1% among the most urban counties&mdash;a gap of 3.1 percentage points. This gradient is consistent: as rurality increases, so does obesity prevalence, suggesting that geographic isolation plays a measurable role in shaping health outcomes.</p></div></div>
    <div class="finding blue"><div class="finding-icon">2</div><div><p><strong>The South and Midwest bear a disproportionate burden.</strong> Counties in the South average 38.7% obesity, while the Midwest averages 38.5%. In stark contrast, Northeastern counties average just 31.5% obesity. Eight of the ten highest-obesity states&mdash;Mississippi (42.6%), Louisiana (42.1%), West Virginia (41.4%), Oklahoma (40.8%), Tennessee (40.0%), Indiana (39.7%), Nebraska (39.4%), and Iowa (39.2%)&mdash;are in these two regions.</p></div></div>
  </div>
</section>

<section id="viz2" class="alt">
  <div class="container">
    <div class="section-label">Interactive Visualization 2</div>
    <h2>Comparing Outcomes Across Groups</h2>
    <p>Toggle the metric and grouping below to explore how obesity and food insecurity vary across rurality quintiles, U.S. regions, and individual states.</p>
    <div class="viz-card">
      <h3>Health Outcomes by Group</h3>
      <p class="viz-desc">Compare how rurality quintiles, regions, and states differ across key health metrics.</p>
      <div class="viz-controls">
        <div><label for="bar-metric">Metric: </label><select id="bar-metric"><option value="obesity">Obesity Rate (%)</option><option value="food_insecure">Food Insecurity (%)</option></select></div>
        <div><label for="bar-view">View: </label><select id="bar-view"><option value="quintile">By Rurality Quintile</option><option value="region">By Region</option><option value="state_top">Top 15 States (Obesity)</option><option value="state_bottom">Bottom 15 States (Obesity)</option></select></div>
      </div>
      <div id="bar-chart" style="width:100%;height:460px;"></div>
    </div>
    <div class="finding green"><div class="finding-icon">3</div><div><p><strong>Food insecurity is the strongest predictor of county-level obesity (r&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.43).</strong> This correlation is substantially stronger than the rurality-obesity link (r&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.30). Among counties where more than 15% of residents are food insecure, the average obesity rate is 41.6%&mdash;compared with 37.2% in counties with lower food insecurity. That 4.4-percentage-point gap underscores how food insecurity functions as a powerful amplifier of poor health outcomes.</p></div></div>
  </div>
</section>

<section id="viz3">
  <div class="container">
    <div class="section-label">Interactive Visualization 3</div>
    <h2>Food Insecurity and Obesity</h2>
    <p>This visualization directly plots food insecurity against obesity rates, with dot size representing the county's rural population percentage. Larger circles represent more rural counties.</p>
    <div class="viz-card">
      <h3>Food Insecurity vs. Obesity</h3>
      <p class="viz-desc">Dot size = rural %. Color = region. Hover for county details.</p>
      <div class="viz-controls">
        <div><label for="scatter2-region">Region: </label><select id="scatter2-region"><option value="All">All Regions</option><option value="South">South</option><option value="Midwest">Midwest</option><option value="Northeast">Northeast</option><option value="West">West</option></select></div>
        <div><label for="scatter2-rural">Rural: </label><select id="scatter2-rural"><option value="All">All Counties</option><option value="rural">Rural (&gt;50%)</option><option value="urban">Urban (&le;50%)</option></select></div>
      </div>
      <div id="scatter-plot2" style="width:100%;height:500px;"></div>
    </div>
    <div class="finding"><div class="finding-icon">4</div><div><p><strong>Rural counties with high food insecurity face a "double burden."</strong> Among the 226 counties that are both majority-rural (&gt;50%) and have high food insecurity (&gt;15%), the average obesity rate is 41.9%&mdash;a full 4.2 percentage points above the national county average of 37.7%. These counties are concentrated in the Mississippi Delta, Appalachia, the Texas-Mexico border region, and tribal lands of the Northern Great Plains. The top 10 highest-obesity counties in the nation are all 100% rural, and 8 of them are in Mississippi or Louisiana.</p></div></div>
  </div>
</section>

<section id="limitations">
  <div class="container narrow">
    <div class="section-label">Limitations</div>
    <h2>What the Data Cannot Tell Us</h2>
    <p>While these patterns are compelling, several important caveats must inform our interpretation of the findings.</p>
    <div class="limits-grid">
      <div class="limit-item"><h4>Correlation, Not Causation</h4><p>This analysis identifies associations, not causal relationships. We cannot conclude that rurality or food insecurity directly cause higher obesity rates. Unmeasured confounding variables&mdash;including income, education, cultural norms, and healthcare access&mdash;may drive the observed patterns.</p></div>
      <div class="limit-item"><h4>Ecological Fallacy</h4><p>County-level aggregation masks significant within-county variation. A county with a high average obesity rate may still have neighborhoods or populations with very low rates. Individual-level conclusions cannot be drawn from aggregate data.</p></div>
      <div class="limit-item"><h4>Self-Reported Data</h4><p>The BRFSS obesity estimates rely on self-reported height and weight, which tend to underestimate true obesity prevalence. This measurement bias may vary across demographic groups and geographies.</p></div>
      <div class="limit-item"><h4>Missing Variables</h4><p>Key factors such as individual exercise habits, food quality, transportation infrastructure, mental health, and the built environment are not captured in this analysis. These factors likely interact with rurality and food insecurity in complex ways.</p></div>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>

<section class="alt">
  <div class="container narrow">
    <div class="section-label">Policy Implications</div>
    <h2>What This Means for Policymakers</h2>
    <p>The geographic clustering of high obesity, food insecurity, and rurality suggests that one-size-fits-all public health interventions may be insufficient. Policymakers should consider place-based strategies that address the compound disadvantages facing rural communities: expanding mobile food markets and grocery incentive programs, investing in transportation infrastructure to reduce geographic isolation, and directing federal nutrition assistance to the specific counties where rurality and food insecurity converge. The data point toward a need for targeted, region-specific interventions&mdash;particularly in the Mississippi Delta, Appalachian region, and tribal communities of the Northern Plains&mdash;rather than broad national campaigns alone.</p>
  </div>
</section>

var counties = COUNTIES.map(function(d) {
  return {fips:d.f, state:d.s, county:d.c, obesity:d.o, rural:d.r, food_insecure:d.fi, lat:d.la, lon:d.lo, region:''};
});

var REGIONS = {
  South:['Alabama','Arkansas','Delaware','Florida','Georgia','Kentucky','Louisiana','Maryland','Mississippi','North Carolina','Oklahoma','South Carolina','Tennessee','Texas','Virginia','West Virginia'],
  Midwest:['Illinois','Indiana','Iowa','Kansas','Michigan','Minnesota','Missouri','Nebraska','North Dakota','Ohio','South Dakota','Wisconsin'],
  Northeast:['Connecticut','Maine','Massachusetts','New Hampshire','New Jersey','New York','Pennsylvania','Rhode Island','Vermont'],
  West:['Alaska','Arizona','California','Colorado','Hawaii','Idaho','Montana','Nevada','New Mexico','Oregon','Utah','Washington','Wyoming']
};
var stateToRegion = {};
Object.keys(REGIONS).forEach(function(r) { REGIONS[r].forEach(function(s) { stateToRegion[s] = r; }); });
counties.forEach(function(c) { c.region = stateToRegion[c.state] || 'Other'; });
var RC = {South:'#C44D2B', Midwest:'#2B6B8C', Northeast:'#5B8C3E', West:'#D4A03C', Other:'#888'};

// Populate state selects
var allStates = [];
var seen = {};
counties.forEach(function(c) { if (!seen[c.state]) { seen[c.state] = true; allStates.push(c.state); } });
allStates.sort();
var allSelects = document.querySelectorAll('#state-filter,.state-sel');
for (var si = 0; si < allSelects.length; si++) {
  for (var sj = 0; sj < allStates.length; sj++) {
    var o = document.createElement('option');
    o.value = allStates[sj];
    o.textContent = allStates[sj];
    allSelects[si].appendChild(o);
  }
}

var plotFont = {family:'DM Sans,sans-serif', size:11, color:'#444'};

function linReg(xs, ys) {
  var n = xs.length;
  if (n < 2) return {m:0, b:0, r:0};
  var sx=0,sy=0,sxy=0,sxx=0,syy=0;
  for (var i=0; i<n; i++) { sx+=xs[i]; sy+=ys[i]; sxy+=xs[i]*ys[i]; sxx+=xs[i]*xs[i]; syy+=ys[i]*ys[i]; }
  var m = (n*sxy - sx*sy) / (n*sxx - sx*sx);
  var b = (sy - m*sx) / n;
  var num = n*sxy - sx*sy;
  var den = Math.sqrt((n*sxx - sx*sx) * (n*syy - sy*sy));
  var r = den ? num/den : 0;
  return {m:m, b:b, r:r};
}

function filterCounties(regionId, stateId) {
  var region = document.getElementById(regionId).value;
  var state = document.getElementById(stateId).value;
  var f = counties;
  if (region !== 'All') f = f.filter(function(c) { return c.region === region; });
  if (state !== 'All') f = f.filter(function(c) { return c.state === state; });
  return f;
}

var OB_SCALE = [[0,'#FFF9C4'],[0.25,'#FFE082'],[0.5,'#FF8F00'],[0.75,'#E65100'],[1,'#4E0000']];
var RU_SCALE = [[0,'#E8F5E9'],[0.25,'#A5D6A7'],[0.5,'#43A047'],[0.75,'#1B5E20'],[1,'#0A280E']];
var FI_SCALE = [[0,'#E3F2FD'],[0.25,'#90CAF9'],[0.5,'#1E88E5'],[0.75,'#0D47A1'],[1,'#051B3E']];

function makeMap(divId, data, valKey, colorscale, title, cmin, cmax) {
  var trace = {
    type:'scattergeo', locationmode:'USA-states',
    lat: data.map(function(c){return c.lat;}),
    lon: data.map(function(c){return c.lon;}),
    marker: {
      size:4, opacity:0.7,
      color: data.map(function(c){return c[valKey];}),
      colorscale: colorscale, cmin:cmin, cmax:cmax,
      colorbar: {title:{text:title,font:{size:9}}, thickness:10, len:0.75, x:1.01}
    },
    text: data.map(function(c){return '<b>'+c.county+', '+c.state+'</b><br>'+title+': '+c[valKey]+'%';}),
    hoverinfo:'text'
  };
  var layout = {
    geo: {scope:'usa', showland:true, landcolor:'#f5f3f0', showlakes:true, lakecolor:'#e8e8e8', subunitcolor:'#ddd', showsubunits:true, bgcolor:'rgba(0,0,0,0)', projection:{type:'albers usa'}},
    margin:{t:5,r:35,b:5,l:5}, height:270,
    paper_bgcolor:'rgba(0,0,0,0)', plot_bgcolor:'rgba(0,0,0,0)', font:plotFont
  };
  Plotly.newPlot(divId, [trace], layout, {responsive:true, displayModeBar:false});
}

function makeScatter(divId, data, xKey, yKey, xLabel, yLabel, dotColor) {
  var xs = data.map(function(c){return c[xKey];});
  var ys = data.map(function(c){return c[yKey];});
  var lr = linReg(xs, ys);
  var xMin = Math.min.apply(null, xs);
  var xMax = Math.max.apply(null, xs);

  var dots = {
    x:xs, y:ys, mode:'markers', type:'scatter', name:'Counties',
    marker:{size:4, color:dotColor, opacity:0.35, line:{width:0.3, color:'rgba(0,0,0,0.1)'}},
    text: data.map(function(c){return '<b>'+c.county+', '+c.state+'</b><br>'+xLabel+': '+c[xKey]+'%<br>'+yLabel+': '+c[yKey]+'%';}),
    hoverinfo:'text'
  };
  var trend = {
    x:[xMin, xMax], y:[lr.m*xMin+lr.b, lr.m*xMax+lr.b],
    mode:'lines', type:'scatter', name:'Trend (r='+lr.r.toFixed(2)+')',
    line:{color:'#222', width:2.5, dash:'dot'}
  };
  var layout = {
    xaxis:{title:xLabel+' (%)', gridcolor:'#eee', zerolinecolor:'#ddd'},
    yaxis:{title:yLabel+' (%)', gridcolor:'#eee', zerolinecolor:'#ddd'},
    margin:{t:12,r:12,b:48,l:48}, height:550,
    paper_bgcolor:'#fff', plot_bgcolor:'#FAFAFA', font:plotFont, hovermode:'closest',
    legend:{x:0.02,y:0.98,bgcolor:'rgba(255,255,255,0.85)',bordercolor:'#ddd',borderwidth:1},
    annotations:[{x:0.98,y:0.02,xref:'paper',yref:'paper',text:'r = '+lr.r.toFixed(3),showarrow:false,font:{size:14,color:'#333',family:'Source Serif 4'},bgcolor:'rgba(255,255,255,0.8)',borderpad:5}]
  };
  Plotly.newPlot(divId, [dots, trend], layout, {responsive:true, displayModeBar:false});
}

// SCATTER 1
function renderScatter1() {
  var region = document.getElementById('region-filter').value;
  var state = document.getElementById('state-filter').value;
  var fi = document.getElementById('fi-filter').value;
  var f = counties;
  if (region !== 'All') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.region===region;});
  if (state !== 'All') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.state===state;});
  if (fi === 'low') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.food_insecure<8;});
  else if (fi === 'med') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.food_insecure>=8 && c.food_insecure<=15;});
  else if (fi === 'high') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.food_insecure>15;});

  var trace = {
    x:f.map(function(c){return c.rural;}), y:f.map(function(c){return c.obesity;}),
    mode:'markers', type:'scatter',
    marker:{size:5, color:f.map(function(c){return c.food_insecure;}),
      colorscale:[[0,'#FFF3E0'],[0.25,'#FFAB91'],[0.5,'#E64A19'],[1,'#4A0000']],
      cmin:0, cmax:25, opacity:0.55,
      colorbar:{title:{text:'Food\nInsecurity %',font:{size:10}},thickness:13,len:0.55},
      line:{width:0.3,color:'rgba(0,0,0,0.12)'}},
    text:f.map(function(c){return '<b>'+c.county+', '+c.state+'</b><br>Obesity: '+c.obesity+'%<br>Rural: '+c.rural+'%<br>Food Insecure: '+c.food_insecure+'%';}),
    hoverinfo:'text'
  };
  Plotly.newPlot('scatter-plot',[trace],{
    xaxis:{title:'Rural Population (%)',range:[-5,105],gridcolor:'#eee'},
    yaxis:{title:'Adult Obesity Rate (%)',range:[15,55],gridcolor:'#eee'},
    margin:{t:12,r:75,b:48,l:48},plot_bgcolor:'#FAFAFA',paper_bgcolor:'#FFF',font:plotFont,hovermode:'closest'
  },{responsive:true,displayModeBar:true,modeBarButtonsToRemove:['lasso2d','select2d']});
}
document.getElementById('region-filter').addEventListener('change', renderScatter1);
document.getElementById('state-filter').addEventListener('change', renderScatter1);
document.getElementById('fi-filter').addEventListener('change', renderScatter1);
renderScatter1();

// BAR CHART
function renderBar() {
  var metric = document.getElementById('bar-metric').value;
  var view = document.getElementById('bar-view').value;
  var mL = {obesity:'Obesity Rate (%)', food_insecure:'Food Insecurity (%)'};
  var labels, values, colors;

  if (view === 'quintile') {
    labels = QUINTILES.map(function(q){return q.label;});
    values = QUINTILES.map(function(q){return q[metric];});
    colors = ['#5B8C3E','#7DAF5D','#BDCC7A','#E8946A','#C44D2B'];
  } else if (view === 'region') {
    var ra = {};
    counties.forEach(function(c){ if(!ra[c.region])ra[c.region]=[]; ra[c.region].push(c[metric]); });
    var entries = Object.keys(ra).map(function(r){ var v=ra[r]; return {n:r, a:v.reduce(function(a,b){return a+b;},0)/v.length}; });
    entries.sort(function(a,b){return b.a-a.a;});
    labels = entries.map(function(e){return e.n;});
    values = entries.map(function(e){return +e.a.toFixed(1);});
    colors = labels.map(function(l){return RC[l]||'#888';});
  } else if (view === 'state_top') {
    var s = STATES_DATA.slice().sort(function(a,b){return b[metric]-a[metric];}).slice(0,15);
    labels = s.map(function(x){return x.state;});
    values = s.map(function(x){return x[metric];});
    colors = s.map(function(x){return RC[x.region]||'#888';});
  } else {
    var s = STATES_DATA.slice().sort(function(a,b){return a[metric]-b[metric];}).slice(0,15);
    labels = s.map(function(x){return x.state;});
    values = s.map(function(x){return x[metric];});
    colors = s.map(function(x){return RC[x.region]||'#888';});
  }

  Plotly.newPlot('bar-chart',[{x:labels,y:values,type:'bar',
    marker:{color:colors,opacity:0.85},
    text:values.map(function(v){return v.toFixed(1)+'%';}), textposition:'outside',
    textfont:{size:11,family:'DM Sans'},
    hovertemplate:'%{x}<br>'+mL[metric]+': %{y:.1f}%<extra></extra>'
  }],{
    yaxis:{title:mL[metric],gridcolor:'#eee'},
    xaxis:{tickangle:view.indexOf('state')>=0?-45:0},
    margin:{t:12,r:15,b:view.indexOf('state')>=0?120:80,l:50},
    plot_bgcolor:'#FAFAFA',paper_bgcolor:'#FFF',font:plotFont,bargap:0.3,hovermode:'closest'
  },{responsive:true,displayModeBar:false});
}
document.getElementById('bar-metric').addEventListener('change', renderBar);
document.getElementById('bar-view').addEventListener('change', renderBar);
renderBar();

// SCATTER 2
function renderScatter2() {
  var region = document.getElementById('scatter2-region').value;
  var rf = document.getElementById('scatter2-rural').value;
  var f = counties;
  if (region !== 'All') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.region===region;});
  if (rf === 'rural') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.rural>50;});
  else if (rf === 'urban') f = f.filter(function(c){return c.rural<=50;});

  var rg = {};
  f.forEach(function(c){ if(!rg[c.region])rg[c.region]=[]; rg[c.region].push(c); });

  var traces = Object.keys(rg).map(function(reg){
    var cs = rg[reg];
    return {
      x:cs.map(function(c){return c.food_insecure;}),
      y:cs.map(function(c){return c.obesity;}),
      mode:'markers',type:'scatter',name:reg,
      marker:{size:cs.map(function(c){return Math.max(4,Math.sqrt(c.rural)*1.3);}),color:RC[reg],opacity:0.4,line:{width:0.3,color:'rgba(0,0,0,0.1)'}},
      text:cs.map(function(c){return '<b>'+c.county+', '+c.state+'</b><br>Obesity: '+c.obesity+'%<br>Food Insecure: '+c.food_insecure+'%<br>Rural: '+c.rural+'%';}),
      hoverinfo:'text'
    };
  });
  Plotly.newPlot('scatter-plot2',traces,{
    xaxis:{title:'Food Insecurity (%)',range:[-1,30],gridcolor:'#eee'},
    yaxis:{title:'Adult Obesity Rate (%)',range:[15,55],gridcolor:'#eee'},
    margin:{t:12,r:12,b:48,l:48},plot_bgcolor:'#FAFAFA',paper_bgcolor:'#FFF',font:plotFont,
    legend:{x:0.78,y:0.98,bgcolor:'rgba(255,255,255,0.85)',bordercolor:'#ddd',borderwidth:1},hovermode:'closest'
  },{responsive:true,displayModeBar:true,modeBarButtonsToRemove:['lasso2d','select2d']});
}
document.getElementById('scatter2-region').addEventListener('change', renderScatter2);
document.getElementById('scatter2-rural').addEventListener('change', renderScatter2);
renderScatter2();

// DASHBOARD RENDERERS
function renderDash1() {
  var d = filterCounties('d1-region','d1-state');
  makeMap('d1-map1',d,'obesity',OB_SCALE,'Obesity %',19,53);
  makeMap('d1-map2',d,'rural',RU_SCALE,'Rural %',0,100);
  makeScatter('d1-scatter',d,'rural','obesity','Rural Population','Adult Obesity Rate','#C44D2B');
}
function renderDash2() {
  var d = filterCounties('d2-region','d2-state');
  makeMap('d2-map1',d,'obesity',OB_SCALE,'Obesity %',19,53);
  makeMap('d2-map2',d,'food_insecure',FI_SCALE,'Food Insecure %',0,25);
  makeScatter('d2-scatter',d,'food_insecure','obesity','Food Insecurity','Adult Obesity Rate','#2B6B8C');
}
function renderDash3() {
  var d = filterCounties('d3-region','d3-state');
  makeMap('d3-map1',d,'rural',RU_SCALE,'Rural %',0,100);
  makeMap('d3-map2',d,'food_insecure',FI_SCALE,'Food Insecure %',0,25);
  makeScatter('d3-scatter',d,'rural','food_insecure','Rural Population','Food Insecurity','#5B8C3E');
}

document.getElementById('d1-region').addEventListener('change', renderDash1);
document.getElementById('d1-state').addEventListener('change', renderDash1);
document.getElementById('d2-region').addEventListener('change', renderDash2);
document.getElementById('d2-state').addEventListener('change', renderDash2);
document.getElementById('d3-region').addEventListener('change', renderDash3);
document.getElementById('d3-state').addEventListener('change', renderDash3);

// Lazy load dashboards when scrolled into view
var d1Done=false, d2Done=false, d3Done=false;
function checkVis() {
  var wh = window.innerHeight;
  if (!d1Done) { var el=document.getElementById('d1-map1'); if(el && el.getBoundingClientRect().top < wh+200) { d1Done=true; renderDash1(); } }
  if (!d2Done) { var el=document.getElementById('d2-map1'); if(el && el.getBoundingClientRect().top < wh+200) { d2Done=true; renderDash2(); } }
  if (!d3Done) { var el=document.getElementById('d3-map1'); if(el && el.getBoundingClientRect().top < wh+200) { d3Done=true; renderDash3(); } }
  if (d1Done && d2Done && d3Done) window.removeEventListener('scroll', checkVis);
}
window.addEventListener('scroll', checkVis);
setTimeout(checkVis, 500);
</script>
</body>
</html>
